    <a title="kari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2207055-kari"><img alt="kari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262446392p2/2207055.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/579679778?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="kari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="kari" href="/user/show/2207055-kari">kari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">no one</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2207055-kari?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2207055-kari?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer579679778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18385596680774838904">Don’t you just love it when you get to the end of a series, close that back cover, sigh contentedly, think of stars and sunshine, regret that you no longer get to spend time in that world with those characters, but feel enclosed in a shining bubble of contentment and happiness for that wonderful ending, hugging the book with joy? <br/>Well, if that is what you’re hoping for with this book, you are in for one whopping disappointment, my friend.<br/>Nothing and I mean a sum total of not a single thing, is a</span>
  <span id="freeText18385596680774838904" style="display:none">Don’t you just love it when you get to the end of a series, close that back cover, sigh contentedly, think of stars and sunshine, regret that you no longer get to spend time in that world with those characters, but feel enclosed in a shining bubble of contentment and happiness for that wonderful ending, hugging the book with joy? <br />Well, if that is what you’re hoping for with this book, you are in for one whopping disappointment, my friend.<br />Nothing and I mean a sum total of not a single thing, is actually resolved or completed or even just finished. I'm curious whether or not this was going to be the ending before this series was picked up for television. <br />How can this series be just this, a love triangle that has a kind of sort of, but who knows, resolution, maybe? How could this happen? That is a serious question. I truly don’t understand what happened.<br />Let me just describe something that happened the other day and see how you feel. Okay, ready?<br />“So, getting out of bed, looked out at the red-streaked sky, reminding me of the blood-shot eyes of my Uncle Morty who always smells of elderberries and turpentine when we would visit him down the Jersey shore where he has lived since retiring from his job at the pickle factory, went downstairs and had breakfast. Getting my bicycle with the red string on the handlebars so as not to confuse it with my best friend’s identical bicycle that does not have string, I rode east to Jones Road, continuing south until I turned left onto Smith Boulevard where the houses start to look somewhat shabby. I went on until I came to a small alley between a boarded up chiropodist, no one cares for their feet these days, and a grocery. I went down the alley emerging on Adams Avenue where I once met a boy with freckles who smiled at me making me think of swimming in the warm waters of the bay with the salty spray splashing in my eyes and followed Adams until I finally turned west toward the better areas of town where the houses are bigger and better kept.”<br />Is that interesting? Or are you saying quit wasting my time and tell the story already? Well, that is the story, my bicycling trip. Wait, you thought it might be about the strange world I'm living in, my fight for survival? No, it is about where I go and how I get there, what streets I take and how I feel going there, how the air smells, how I enjoy the wind in my face, the bumpy or smooth pavement, the taste of the salt spray as I near the ocean, the creaking of the trees, the birdsong or lack of birdsong, my commentary on the housing.<br />Is this off subject? NO. My point is that in this whole series there is tons of bicycling, walking, trudging through the woods/Wilds, driving(Hana) and just droning on and on about things that are so boring and add not one iota to the story. Do you really care what street she is on? Or how the houses look, for the fifteenth time? Or how the trudging in the woods today feels different from the trudging in the woods yesterday or last week? In fact, I’d say that if all of that minutiae was removed or even mildly tightened, what you’d have here would be one book instead of three. <br />Please note, that I did not say one GOOD book, but just one book.<br />Okay, back on track. <br />I began this trilogy/misery because I read Before I Fall and thought Oliver had something special to her writing. Now, I just think she has wasted my time with this drivel about nothing more than a love triangle and not one that was EVER believable.<br />I want characters who grow during the course of a story, whether a single book or a series. Growth. Change. Dare I say, even maturity.<br />None of that happens here and, in my opinion, Lena becomes much less of an admirable person by the series end than in the beginning. Oh, is that the overall message? Love makes you into a selfish user? How sad.<br />Her constant use of Julian to make herself feel better about Alex, how are we supposed to congratulate her for that? Oh, well done you, Lena. <br />One of the things I liked the very least was that she spared no time or thought for Alex. Once he was caught she just walked/ran off. This guy gave his life for her, to save her, or so she believes,(She knows better, doesn’t she? She knows her own mother was supposedly immediately executed but in reality survived many years in jail before escaping *Note: And why, exactly is she so pissed off at her mother? It isn’t like she purposely went to jail or that she could have just come home to get Lena when she escaped.*)but she cannot even bother to try to find out if he is alive. <br />I so hoped that the second book would be Lena coming into her own, investigating what happened to Alex, finding a way to free him or at least get a message to him that she is okay. But she leaves him behind like a sweaty pair of gym socks left on the bathroom floor. <br />The third book I was longing to read about Alex and Lena being reunited after his escape(with or without her help) with some resolution to the situation. I would have loved to have some understanding along the way of why their world is at it is. It still makes not one jot of sense that love is outlawed and that the government, which it would seem is struggling to keep peace, feed, house and clothe its citizenry, would waste resources battling with those on the outside who have nothing.<br />What I still don't understand is the reasoning behind love being outlawed. I mean, if you really wanted to solve the society/world's problems why not outlaw hate? If you could surgically alter the brain then why would you not get rid of hate? A world without hate = a much better place. And even putting that argument aside, how about just explaining at some point WHY this decision was made? Nothing in this world makes the first bit of sense. <br />And, why would those who don't want to be cured be any kind of a threat to the government that they would waste time killing them? I mean, these people DON'T EVEN HAVE EATING UTENSILS!!! IF they can't even organize themselves enough to find some spoons, for gosh sakes, then they probably pose no threat to the government if left alone. Does this make any kind of sense at all? No, it really doesn't. I think I am the most disgusted with this series as I thought it held a lot of promise. Now, not so much.<br />And the love triangle. Not for one single minute did I ever believe in the love between Julian and Lena. It never worked because it was so obvious he was nothing more than a stand-in, shoved at us in the second book. Yes, I did say shoved because it is so handy that Lena just happened to be conveniently imprisoned with Julian, the first not-gay or attached boy she's been alone with since leaving civilization. The depth of her feelings would seem to be oh, I'm here and he's here and what was the name of that guy who DIED FOR ME, the guy whom I can't even seem to remember that I liked or that he existed?<br />Additionally, Lena never does anything that isn’t in her own interest. She doesn’t grow and care about the world around her. She cares about herself and what she needs. Perhaps that is human nature and that is what we all do, I don't know. She doesn’t cling to Julian out of love for him or because he needs her, but because he makes her feel better over Alex. Blech.<br />Until there is this epiphany, page 328: "I will never love Julian like I love Alex." What a surprise. Didn't we know that all along? For gosh sakes, she is stupid, too stupid to realize that the boy who was willing to give up his life for her, who was shot while saving her, was imprisoned, was <i>tortured</i>, just might be a little bit irritated to see her show up all kissy-face with a new guy within <i>months</i> of losing him. And that this boy might then say something to hurt her, something like that he never loved her. Idiot.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ And Julian gets the crap kicked out of himself because he <i>attacks Alex</i>, not the other way around, but does Lena get angry at Julian for beinng a hot-headed jerk. No, of course not. She lets loose on Alex, without ever knowing what he has been through and taking a moment to understand what being attacked might mean from his viewpoint. And let me say again, Julian attacked him. So Alex shouldn't have protected himself?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />During the big battle she isn’t planning to help, but to go off and do what she wants. She doesn’t consider if that action will be good for those involved or cause them harm, but it is what she wants.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ And the moment when the battle is starting and Oliver must have simply gone “Eenie, meenie, miney, moe, which character should I kill here about which Lena can think about for the blink of an eye before she goes back to her own needs? And it had to be RAVEN??? All these others that we couldn't care less about, but she decides to do in Raven<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[who, if you read the short story about her, was pregnant <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Really? Why not off Coral who was ever just there for the romantic angst and served no other purpose?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />There are two perspectives to the story: Lena and Hana. The reason I almost gave this two stars instead of one is that, the two POVs, was a good idea. Hana's is actually the more interesting of the two, in my opinion, although I don't like Hana so tough to feel too sorry for her. Yep, I guessed what she had done waaaaaaaaaay back when.<br />All in all, this series is a supreme waste of time and paper. I had high hopes for it, but was completely let down and I doubt I’d be convinced to read this author again.<br />Sorry this review is so rambling, but my disgust is so great that it was hard to organize my thoughts effectively.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18385596680774838904" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11100515554281235465">2.5 stars.<br/><br/>I'm not sure I know what to say about this one. <br/><br/>While I was only mildly impressed with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136767171' rel='nofollow noopener'>Delirium</a>, and found Lena to be a weak and indecisive character, I was incredibly impressed with her development in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160832928' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pandemonium</a>. Lena grew into a strong, determined character, with a cause far greater than somewhat ordinary teenage love. <br/><br/>In <i>Requiem</i> all the momentum built in <i>Pandemonium</i> was halted. Despite the all out war brewing between the Regulators and the Invalids, the main focus of the story was </span>
  <span id="freeText11100515554281235465" style="display:none">2.5 stars.<br /><br />I'm not sure I know what to say about this one. <br /><br />While I was only mildly impressed with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136767171" rel="nofollow noopener">Delirium</a>, and found Lena to be a weak and indecisive character, I was incredibly impressed with her development in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160832928" rel="nofollow noopener">Pandemonium</a>. Lena grew into a strong, determined character, with a cause far greater than somewhat ordinary teenage love. <br /><br />In <i>Requiem</i> all the momentum built in <i>Pandemonium</i> was halted. Despite the all out war brewing between the Regulators and the Invalids, the main focus of the story was Lena's feelings for Alex and Julian--which changed every other chapter or so. <br /><br />I found <i>Requiem</i> to be incredibly flat and boring, even with the many fighting scenes. They all seemed recycled, and took a backseat to Lena's dithering about the two boys. <br /><br />And the ending? The nicest word I have for it is abrupt. All in all, a disappointing conclusion to a promising series.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Lena spent the entire story thinking about Alex. How she felt about him. How he might feel for her. How he felt for someone else. Meanwhile, she's still stringing Julian along, one minute running into his arms, the next emasculating him in front of their entire group. It was obvious she didn't respect Julian, and was using him to make Alex jealous, or to make herself feel better when Alex shunned her.<br /><br />And despite having maybe two actual conversations in the entire book, neither of which what you might call nice, when Alex says he still loves her that's it? That's the end of the whole story? The happy ending? We don't even get to see what happens with Julian, if he lives or dies? What happens with the Resistance? Nope. Alex and Lena are back together, so obviously everything's gonna be fine. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /> </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie" href="/user/show/9282548-jamie">Jamie</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer4864666321149165553">********Warning, spoilers for Pandemonium in passage below*********<br/><br/>I'm gonna be blunt and put it out there. I don't like Julian. Sure, he's nice and all that, but he's not Alex. Julian is sheltered and too much of an important figure to be involved in Lena's romantic affairs. He's inexperienced, knows nothing on how to survive in The Wild. While Alex helped Lena, Julian is the one that needs the taking care of. He's much weaker than Alex. <br/>My heart literally skipped like 5 beats when I read the e</span>
  <span id="freeText4864666321149165553" style="display:none">********Warning, spoilers for Pandemonium in passage below*********<br /><br />I'm gonna be blunt and put it out there. I don't like Julian. Sure, he's nice and all that, but he's not Alex. Julian is sheltered and too much of an important figure to be involved in Lena's romantic affairs. He's inexperienced, knows nothing on how to survive in The Wild. While Alex helped Lena, Julian is the one that needs the taking care of. He's much weaker than Alex. <br />My heart literally skipped like 5 beats when I read the ending of Pandemonium. It went pang, and it was like I saw his hair and heard his low voice. <br />I guess I knew all along that Alex wasn't dead. It was a small, hopeful spark in my heart and when Julian came into the story I got kinda mad. I'm kinda attached to Alex, alright? <br />All I can think about right now is the word "Run" that Alex said when he was caught. Not "Save me" but "Run". He sacrificed his life for her and didn't think once about himself. No wonder his eyes were all stony when he caught them kissing and making promises. <br />Last of all, I cannot believe I have to wait another year for the third book. <br />Lena better get back with Alex, or else. Julian can go marry Sarah or something. </span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=blah">blah</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=cheesy">cheesy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=wtf">wtf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=douchery-afoot">douchery-afoot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer560760707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12111327543107150845"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>I was going to give this one star because the ending was ridiculous, actually the whole book was ridiculous… But because I'm really nice, I decided to add an extra star. <i>Your welcome</i>, Lauren Oliver.<br/><br/>For those who haven't read <i>Requiem</i>. Here's a breakdown:<br/><br/><b>Lena</b>: Alex no dead. What I do? It be painful. <br/><br/><b>Alex</b>: I no dead Lena. You be evul whore. Why you no grieve forever when you be thinking I being dead? I never loving you! I always hating you now!<br/><br/><b>Julian</b>: Huh?<br/><br/><b>Lena</b>: Alex no wuv me. Me so sad. I </span>
  <span id="freeText12111327543107150845" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />I was going to give this one star because the ending was ridiculous, actually the whole book was ridiculous… But because I'm really nice, I decided to add an extra star. <i>Your welcome</i>, Lauren Oliver.<br /><br />For those who haven't read <i>Requiem</i>. Here's a breakdown:<br /><br /><b>Lena</b>: Alex no dead. What I do? It be painful. <br /><br /><b>Alex</b>: I no dead Lena. You be evul whore. Why you no grieve forever when you be thinking I being dead? I never loving you! I always hating you now!<br /><br /><b>Julian</b>: Huh?<br /><br /><b>Lena</b>: Alex no wuv me. Me so sad. I know… I using the Julian, making the Alex jealous. That teach him to no love me.<br /><br /><b>Alex</b>: I like new girl now. It okay I move on with new person but Lena whore for moving on. It no matter she thought I be dead. It no matter at all.<br /><br /><b>Lena</b>: I hate new girl. I act like bitch to everyone because Alex not wanting me. Me being so sad.<br /><br /><b>Julian</b>: Huh?<br /><br /><b>Alex</b>: I run away. I liking the drama. It making me the sexier.<br /><br /><b>Lena</b>: Oh noes! Alex go again. I be so in loving with him. It okay. I still be having the Julian, he be being my backup.<br /><br /><b>Julian</b>: Huh?<br /><br /><b>Lena</b>: I guess I be helping everyone fight bad guys because I being bwave. Why my life so hard? Oh I forgotted my cousin I abandon-did. I be going save her now. <br /><br /><b>Alex</b>: Lena, I be loving you now. You be loving me?<br /><br /><b>Lena</b>: I be loving you but also be loving the Julian. I go now help everyone fight bad guys.<br /><br /><b>Alex</b>: Okay then, I be seeing you.<br /><br /><b>Lena</b>: Bye bye.<br /><br /><b>Julian</b>: Huh?<br /><br />The end.<br /><br /><br /><b>Random notes/thoughts:</b><br /><br />-In the first half Lena and the rest of the Invalids did nothing — they just plodded along in the Wilds arguing about what to do next. All they ended up doing was walking from one place to the next — it was boring. There was more action in the second half when Lena/the Invalids and the Resistance start to fight back — that was a bit more interesting.<br /><br />-Lena and Hana both took turns narrating. I did find their voices quite similar, which shouldn't have been the case 1. Because they were obviously two different characters and 2. Because Hana had the operation to more or less make her emotionless — so either Hana had too much emotion or Lena just had a robotic POV. Even though they sounded similar, Hana was more likeable. <br />I didn't see what Hana's POV added to the overall story — it was just her monologuing about random stuff, getting ready for her wedding and being suspicious of her soon to be husband. It wasn't really needed — it didn't affect Lena's story or the big showdown at the end.<br /><br />-Not enough Lena/Alex scenes.<br /><br />-Lena was immensely unlikeable. She was vile — she's easily one of my most hated YA heroines ever. All she did was whine, feel sorry for herself and bitch about everyone and everything. She treated Julian awfully — if he was being nice to her she would complain, if he wasn't constantly up her arse she'd complain, if he volunteered to do something risky to prove himself she'd complain and if he helped the group she'd complain. She was a bitch.<br />She was completely pathetic and petty when it came to Alex. Instead of fighting for him, she did nothing but whine about him not loving her. And then she'd use Julian to make him jealous — she was awful.<br />She was a total cow to Coral - I wouldn't have minded her vile attitude if Coral had actually done something to deserve it but she hadn't.<br /><br />-I hated Alex too. I could get why he was angry but he still treated Lena like rubbish. She genuinely thought Alex was dead, that's the only reason she moved on. What did he want her to do, grieve for him for the rest of her life? It's obvious that she would never have been with Julian if she suspected he was alive. I found it dumb that he was moaning about Lena moving on yet he had no problem moving on with Coral straight away. He was a hypocrite. <br /><br />-The only characters that were likeable in the ridiculous love square were Julian and Coral - Lena and Alex selfishly used them so they could play games with each other.<br /><br />-The reunion between Lena and Annabel was rubbish. I wanted tears, pain, anger and years of bitterness but all I got was a small hissy fit and then nothing. They literally talked for a couple of minutes and then became best friends. I expected Lena to be angry for a long while but she got over her anger as soon as her mum gave her some half arse, lame non-explanation for abandoning her/not contacting her sooner.<br /><br />-The ending was lame. It literally stopped in a middle of a scene. There was no closure or answers.<br /><br />-Did Raven die? What was the point of making Raven pregnant in her novella when it wasn't bought up or even hinted at in <i>Requiem</i>. It seemed like the only reason Lauren Oliver made her pregnant was so her death could be tragic. Ugh.<br /><br />-The lame love triangle didn't have a satisfying conclusion. Sure, Lena said she loved Alex more than Julian but does that mean she dumped Julian for Alex? I wanted to see a break up scene and a proper reunion scene.<br /><br />-What happened to Rachel? Why didn't Annabel talk about helping Rachel? I know Rachel was cured but why would Annabel still abandon her and not think about her. It was weird. Annabel was a bitch — she just seemed to write off her daughters so she could play hero.<br /><br />-What happened to Jenny and Lena's aunt and uncle?<br /><br />-Was the rest of the world like America?<br /><br />-Did the Invalids and Resistance manage to take over Portland? Or were they beaten? What happened in the other cities?<br /><br />-What happened to Hana? Did her treatment fail? Does she just carry on walking around in her wedding dress for the rest of her life?<br /><br />-What happened to Julian? Wasn't he meant to be dying or something? If Lena dumps him, how does he cope?<br /><br />Just WTF. Either Lauren Oliver couldn't be bothered or she was trying to make the ending high brow and profound or some rubbish. She should have realised that she's writing books that revolve around lame world building, a crappy plot and teenage angst… Not to mention the fact that at least half of her readers were only reading for the love triangle. She's not writing some thought provoking literary masterpiece that's left open ended and mysterious because it suits the theme of book… Nope, she's writing a YA series that's main focus is arguably the love triangle. The least she could have done was give a satisfying resolution to the Alex/Lean/Julian drama. For shame, Lauren Oliver. For shame.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12111327543107150845" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer991042549829242761">For as much shit as the end of this book got from everyone, <br/>I thought it was pretty perfect. I didn't think it was unfair at all. Open, yes, but some easy inferences tell you everything you need to know.<br /><br />I got just what I wanted from my favorite characters, and I won't lie: I was pretty excited about Lena's choice in the end.<br /><br />Oliver's beautiful, beautiful writing never hurts, either. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Lauren Oliver says, in a tweet to me:<br /><br /><b>"I won't say a word! V proud of that book, though. I made some unconventional choices and I'm excited about it"</b><br /><br />AHHH! She made unconventional choices! Don't you love when authors do that and it's not just Mrs. Predictable writing a book?<br /><br />CANNOT WAIT FOR THIS MASTERPIECE TO BE IN MY HOUSE.</span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review135374314">

<span id="freeTextContainer3245877324055721113">Okay ... I just finished reading pandemonium ... literally two seconds ago ... AND<br/><br/>I really really REALLY want her to end up with Julian!!<br/>I dont like Alex(sorry)<br/><br/>With Alex she didnt have to fight it .. she just got swept up in the throes of a whirlwind romance.<br/><br/>With Julian, she fought it, she denied it and she STILL started to fall for him.<br/><br/>She went back for JULIAN! she didnt go back for Alex (speaks volumes me thinks)<br/><br/>When I was reading the Lena/Julian moments I got a warm fuzzy happy feeling in my </span>
  <span id="freeText3245877324055721113" style="display:none">Okay ... I just finished reading pandemonium ... literally two seconds ago ... AND<br /><br />I really really REALLY want her to end up with Julian!!<br />I dont like Alex(sorry)<br /><br />With Alex she didnt have to fight it .. she just got swept up in the throes of a whirlwind romance.<br /><br />With Julian, she fought it, she denied it and she STILL started to fall for him.<br /><br />She went back for JULIAN! she didnt go back for Alex (speaks volumes me thinks)<br /><br />When I was reading the Lena/Julian moments I got a warm fuzzy happy feeling in my chest that I didnt get when I was reading Lena/Alex. <br /><br />And I know that Alex took a few bullets for her and everything ... but chances are he wouldve been able to escape because of the sympathisers. Julian didnt hae that option, he went into that room with the certainty that he would die, and he was willing to die so that he could keep his memories of him and Lena. <br /><br />I was acually kinda gutted when Alex turned up coz now shes going to be all conflicted and crap. When i was reading Delirium Alex didnt melt me the way that Julian did in Pandemonium. I absoultly love how clueless Julian is and yet he still follows Lena blindly ... just like Lena did with Alex. <br /><br />And now that Alex has been all screwed up by the Crypts I dont think he is going to be very nice. I think Lena deserves the safe bet who makes her feel good about herself after everything she has been through and that safe bet is Julian. End Of.<br /><br />Ill be gutted if she ends up with Alex but I am looking forward to her being re-united with her mother.</span>

<div id="review_430601496" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/430601496" />
    <a title="Marina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13500406-marina"><img alt="Marina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361224250p2/13500406.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/430601496?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marina" href="/user/show/13500406-marina">Marina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13500406-marina?shelf=food-for-thought">food-for-thought</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13500406-marina?shelf=kick-ass-heroes-heroines">kick-ass-heroes-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13500406-marina?shelf=dystopia-post-apocalyptic">dystopia-post-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer430601496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11184501833839311063"><b>
  <i>3.5 stars</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/>Well..<br/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380380058ra/736673.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/>I'm going to start pleading my case here.<br/><br/><br/>First of all, I have to admit that I find this a genuinely authentic theme for a dystopian trilogy. Some readers may consider it obscenely absurd. Idiotic. Daft. Pick one.<br/><br/>Not me.<br/><br/>It's actually very clever.<br/><br/><br/>Can you honestly guarantee that with the rate things are going, something like this would be impossible to occur?<br/>I mean, hear this humanity.<br/>If dividing mankind into pre-determined factions to avoid social inconsistencies and emotion</span>
  <span id="freeText11184501833839311063" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>3.5 stars</i>
</b><br><br><br>Well..<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380380058ra/736673.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br><br>I'm going to start pleading my case here.<br><br><br>First of all, I have to admit that I find this a genuinely authentic theme for a dystopian trilogy. Some readers may consider it obscenely absurd. Idiotic. Daft. Pick one.<br><br>Not me.<br><br>It's actually very clever.<br><br><br>Can you honestly guarantee that with the rate things are going, something like this would be impossible to occur?<br>I mean, hear this humanity.<br>If dividing mankind into pre-determined factions to avoid social inconsistencies and emotional fallouts, or throwing together kids in a bloodthirsty arena competition to the death to "teach a lesson" to the disobedient lot does not work out, why not do something like this?<br><br>Why not perform one simple surgery to subdue all feelings of love, compassion, friendship and create one big family of catatonic coach potatoes? There goes your next plan, world.<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380393758ra/758151.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br><br>For me this particular lay-out of the plot worked perfectly.<br>The heroine, <b>Lena</b>, really seems to grasp the seriousness of the situation.<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>My mouth is so dry; the sun is so blinding. I look away, toward the hundreds and hundreds of people who have been<br>driven out of their homes, out of their lives, to this place of dust and dirtiness, all because they wanted the power to feel, to think, to choose for themselves. They couldn’t have known that even this was a lie—that we never really choose, not entirely. We are always being pushed and squeezed down one road or another. We have no choice but to step forward, and then step forward again, and then step forward again; suddenly we find ourselves on a road we haven’t chosen at all.<br>But maybe happiness isn’t in the choosing. Maybe it’s in the fiction, in the pretending: that wherever we have ended up is where we intended to be all along.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><br>But the thing is that, the two previous books built on the fact that this whole resistance, this whole rebellion, had one objective.<br>Being able to choose. To love.<br>And not just love a partner or a husband and a wife.<br>But to love a son, or a daughter, a mother, a sister and so on.<br>People were being persecuted for showing sympathies towards their own kids.<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380393758ra/758152.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br><br>So, where is this element of love in this final book?<br>There is this one love interest, <b>Alex</b>, who is in love with Lena but I just can't see it almost anywhere, and there is this other love interest, <b>Julian</b>, whose love I can see and who ends up alone after choosing to leave behind everything he knew his entire life to chase the freedom of making his own choices.<br><br>So I'm left feeling like:<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391568ra/754067.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br><br>Because the book has ended, and most importantly the trilogy has ended, and I'm thinking:<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/463405.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br><br>Thankfully, the final words somewhat salvage it.<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Take down the walls.<br>That is, after all, the whole point. You do not know what will happen if you take down the walls; you cannot see through to the other side, don’t know whether it will bring freedom or ruin, resolution or chaos. It might be paradise or destruction.<br>Take down the walls.<br>Otherwise you must live closely, in fear, building barricades against the unknown, saying prayers against the darkness, speaking verse of terror and tightness.<br>Otherwise you may never know hell; but you will not find heaven, either. You will not know fresh air and flying.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><br>I guess that's it.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380393758ra/758153.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="11184501833839311063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_313740426" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/313740426" />
    <a title="Shelby Petrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3717818-shelby-petrie"><img alt="Shelby Petrie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452097750p2/3717818.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/313740426?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelby Petrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelby Petrie" href="/user/show/3717818-shelby-petrie">Shelby Petrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer313740426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16807035648823763324">Ok so I found this book to be my second favorite in the series. I still love the first one because, well it HAS Alex in it. The ending wasn't as big or good as I hoped it would be, I hated Julian and I was more than happy when he was kinda shoved out of Lena's heart in the end, but she still wasn't sure who to pick. *cough* Alex *cough*. I loved all the action in this book and cried multiple times. This is one of my favorite love stories because it actually opened my eyes and showed me what love</span>
  <span id="freeText16807035648823763324" style="display:none">Ok so I found this book to be my second favorite in the series. I still love the first one because, well it HAS Alex in it. The ending wasn't as big or good as I hoped it would be, I hated Julian and I was more than happy when he was kinda shoved out of Lena's heart in the end, but she still wasn't sure who to pick. *cough* Alex *cough*. I loved all the action in this book and cried multiple times. This is one of my favorite love stories because it actually opened my eyes and showed me what love really means, that it's just not another feeling or word we coexist next to every day.<br />So I wanna talk about the ending. I feel like Oliver was actually trying to convey a meaning in the way her series ended even though it left us confused. Here is my idea:<br />In the moment, we don’t know where our lives will lead us and we don’t know how things could change tomorrow. But when you’re at a good place, you just have to revel in that moment and let everything come as it may. <br /><br />None the less I think it was still good but the first book: Delirium will ALWAYS be my favorite.(:</span>
  <a data-text-id="16807035648823763324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_538476176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/538476176" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/538476176?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=what-the-hell">what-the-hell</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=no-hell-no">no-hell-no</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=only-when-it-is-for-free">only-when-it-is-for-free</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=chinese-translation">chinese-translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=over-my-dead-body">over-my-dead-body</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=unable-to-suppress-my-disbelief">unable-to-suppress-my-disbelief</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=i-hate-love-triangle">i-hate-love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=nothing-special">nothing-special</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=one-of-the-worst-books-ever">one-of-the-worst-books-ever</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer538476176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7511320542193576553">Starting from the very beginning, I know the world building in the Delirium series is bullshit, the setting that love is now being treated by a dysptoian American government as an illness is bullshit, I also know that the story is more about a teenage love triangle among Alex/Lena/Julian than the long-suffering citizens fighting the evil government, I also know that the characters are only "Meh" at best.<br/><br/>So why was I still reading? It's because the second book of the series is quite okay-ish and </span>
  <span id="freeText7511320542193576553" style="display:none">Starting from the very beginning, I know the world building in the Delirium series is bullshit, the setting that love is now being treated by a dysptoian American government as an illness is bullshit, I also know that the story is more about a teenage love triangle among Alex/Lena/Julian than the long-suffering citizens fighting the evil government, I also know that the characters are only "Meh" at best.<br /><br />So why was I still reading? It's because the second book of the series is quite okay-ish and I was hoping the final book would redeem the series for me, but it doesn't!<br /><br /><i>Requiem</i> sucks on so many levels. I would have ranted on and on about all the messed up little details and failure which pissed me off and made me go <i>"What. The. Fuck?"</i> when reading the book. But I soon realized this book doesn't deserve that much of my time and effort. <br /><br />I can tell you that: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12383869-sever" rel="nofollow noopener">Sever</a>, the finale of The Chemical Garden trilogy, despite of all its failure in world building, weak heroine and other flaws, the author of that book actually managed to wrap things up, whilst as Lauren Oliver doesn't seem to be able to do so. <br /><br />I will do a break down here:<br /><br />(1) Lena, make up your damn mind on whom you want to be with!<br /><br />(2) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Alex! You're an asshole! Lena thought you were dead and what did you expect her to do? Grieving over you for the rest of her life!? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />(3) The love triangle is unnecessary, who has time for this shit when they are on the run for their lives and the soldiers all have an 'search and destroy' order when it comes to the Invalids? <br /><br />(4) The author doesn't bother to wrap up all the loosen ends. What happens to Lena's older sister, her uncle and aunt? Who does Lena choose in the end? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(It's hinted that she chose Alex, but still) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Who had made it out of the battle alive and who hadn't? What happens to the rest of the America? What is going to happen to all the 'cured' citizens? No answer at all.<br /><br />(5) Everything feels very rushed, and the emotion isn't built up properly, not at all. <br /><br />You know what!? I would actually like a dystopian novel with <i>"people fought, people died fighting, the rebels took down the evil government, and they finally saw the beginning of a new world"</i> as its ending and conclusion, I suspect Ms. Oliver was trying to end her book with something similar. <br /><br />However, the ending of <i>Requiem</i> fails to work because everything is too rushed, the emotion isn't built up finely, so many things are left unexplained or unsolved, so many supporting characters just vanish without any mention, and there're too little fighting for the story's heroine. Ms. Oliver, that isn't how this story should end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7511320542193576553" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_330051612" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/330051612" />
    <a title="Allison Mcswain" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4683808-allison-mcswain"><img alt="Allison Mcswain" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1292864934p2/4683808.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/330051612?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison Mcswain" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison Mcswain" href="/user/show/4683808-allison-mcswain">Allison Mcswain</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer330051612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11936326460833499">SO DISAPPOINTED <br/>I love Lauren Oliver's writing, but I feel that Pandemonium deserved to be followed with something better--something less rushed.<br/>It's the curse of the third and final book. I hated Mockingjay because it was so rushed (like, oh, it's the final book, let's get it over with). I thought Lauren wouldn't let that happen...but I feel it did. Requiem was rushed and left me unsatisfied. <br/>This series WAS my favorite...but this ruined it. Still love the first two books. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wTmq8VYTQbV715sePcs9HGOoC0YKiQ7QYwpa/vbWoNH7H8Mj7U2I3dz8L3/KPjfDtffsjsQEgLc4dBxPO5VSSw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IFgZUJhpfh9DTy1+PNArF2J9NR8gniK73o8fe54csy8afnCCIze3d+RkmR/LJSHItCLS1+4TrNyF8VnKU19BtQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer811419547285898043">Lauren Oliver is the cofounder of media and content development company Glasstown Entertainment, where she serves as the president of production. She is also the New York Times bestselling author of the YA novels Replica, Vanishing Girls, Panic, and the Delirium trilogy: Delirium, Pandemonium, and Requiem, which have been translated into more than thirty languages. The film rights to both Replica </span>
  <span id="freeText811419547285898043" style="display:none">Lauren Oliver is the cofounder of media and content development company Glasstown Entertainment, where she serves as the president of production. She is also the New York Times bestselling author of the YA novels Replica, Vanishing Girls, Panic, and the Delirium trilogy: Delirium, Pandemonium, and Requiem, which have been translated into more than thirty languages. The film rights to both Replica and Lauren's bestselling first novel, Before I Fall, were acquired by AwesomenessTV; Before I Fall is now a major motion picture and opened in theaters March of 2017. The sequel to Replica, titled Ringer, is her most recent novel and was released October 3rd, 2017.<br /><br />Her novels for middle grade readers include The Spindlers, Liesl &amp; Po, and the Curiosity House series, co-written with H. C. Chester. She has written one novel for adults, Rooms.<br /><br />A graduate of the University of Chicago and NYU's MFA program, Lauren Oliver divides her time between New York, Connecticut, and a variety of airport lounges. You can visit her online at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.laurenoliverbooks.com">www.laurenoliverbooks.com</a>.</span>

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Take down the walls. <br />That is, after all, the whole point. <br />You do not know what will happen if you take down the walls; you cannot see through to the other side, don't know whether it will bring freedom or ruin, resolution or chaos. It might be paradise or destruction. <br />Take down the walls.<br />Otherwise you must live closely, in fear, building barricades against the unknown, saying prayers against the darkness, speaking verse of terror and tightness.<br />Otherwise you may never know hell; but you will not find heaven, either. You will not know fresh air and flying.<br />All of you, wherever you are: in your spiny cities, or your one bump towns. Find it, the hard stuff, the links of metal and chink, the fragments of stone filling you stomach. <br />And pull, and pull, and pull.<br />I will make a pact with you: I will do it if you will do it, always and forever.<br />Take down the walls.&rdquo;</span>
